{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01WAqeHNhb4aA6zr4NgtiH9m","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I found the critical piece. Line 64 shows that the xDS layer calls `proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config)` to determine whether a proxy should receive a push for a config change. This is where the issue manifests.\n\nNow let me look at the DependsOnConfig function more closely, which I already saw in sidecar.go (lines 523-540).\n\nNow I have a good understanding of the issue. Let me trace through the flow:\n\n1. **Setting up the configuration (lines from multiple files)**:\n   - In `sidecar.go`, `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterate through destination rules and add their ConfigKeys to `configDependencies`\n   - Lines 219-227 and 410-416 show this code adding dependencies\n\n2. **The problem is in the mergeDestinationRule function in destination_rule.go**:\n   - When two DestinationRules for the same host are merged, they are stored together in a list\n   - The `destRuleConfig` passed in has metadata with a specific Name and Namespace\n   - But when merging, the function modifies the destination rule in-place (or deep copies it), keeping only one set of metadata\n\n3. **How the dependency tracking breaks**:\n   - In `sidecar.go` lines 219-227 and 410-416, the code iterates through `out.destinationRules[hostname]`\n   - Each `dr` in the iteration should be a separate DestinationRule with its own Name and Namespace metadata\n   - But wait, actually looking at the code more carefully, it does iterate through the list\n\nLet me look more carefully at the mergeDestinationRule function again. The key part is around line 65-67:\n```go\ncopied := mdr.DeepCopy()\np.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n\n\nmergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n```\n\nAnd then around line 101-103:\n```go\nif addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n    p.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n}\n```\n\nSo when there are multiple DRs for the same host, the function either merges the incoming rule into an existing one (when `addRuleToProcessedDestRules` is false) or appends it as a separate entry. This means the list can contain multiple DestinationRules, each with their own metadata that should be tracked as separate dependencies.\n\nThe problem emerges when two DRs without workload selectors are processed sequentially. The second one gets merged into the first instead of being kept as a distinct entry, causing the second DR's metadata to be lost. For example, if DR-1 defines traffic policies and DR-2 adds subsets, both without workload selectors, DR-2 gets absorbed into DR-1 during processing. When DR-2 is later updated, the system doesn't recognize it as a separate rule that needs reprocessing.\n\nThe push event for the updated DR-2 references its ConfigKey, but that key was never registered as a dependency—only DR-1's key was tracked. So when the dependency check runs, it fails to find DR-2 in the configDependencies map, and the update gets skipped entirely. The root cause traces back to how SetDestinationRules in push_context.go calls mergeDestinationRule, which determines whether configs are merged or kept separate based on workload selector matching. ationRule)\n    bothWithoutSelector := rule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil && existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil\n    bothWithSelector := existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil\n    selectorsMatch := labels.Instance(existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels()).Equals(rule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\n\n    if bothWithSelector && !selectorsMatch {\n        // If the new destination rule and the existing one has workload selectors associated with them, skip merging\n        // if the selectors do not match\n        continue\n    }\n\n    // If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\n    // If the incoming rule has a workload selector, it has to be merged with the existing rules with workload selector\n\nThe merge logic checks whether workload selectors exist and whether they match. When both rules have selectors that don't align, the loop skips to the next rule. Otherwise, if neither has a selector or the selectors match, the rules can be merged together. Let me think through what happens in this scenario. When DR-1 is processed first, it gets added to the list since there's no existing rule for that host. Then DR-2 comes in and matches DR-1 because they share the same host and both lack workload selectors, so the merge happens—DR-2's subsets get folded into DR-1 and DR-2 itself isn't added as a separate entry. This leaves p.destRules[hostname] containing only the merged rule. Later, when SidecarScope builds, it iterates through that single merged rule and adds its ConfigKey to the scope.\n\nThe problem emerges when DR-2 gets updated. The xDS layer triggers a ConfigUpdate for DR-2's ConfigKey, but the SidecarProxy's DependsOnConfig only tracks DR-1's ConfigKey since that's the only one registered during the scope build. ConfigAffectsProxy returns false, so the proxy never gets notified of the change.\n\nThere's a subtlety here though—when the merge happens, the existing rule gets modified in place, but its metadata (Name and Namespace) stays unchanged. The config.Config object retains its original identity even though its Spec has been updated with the merged content.\n\nLooking at the actual merge implementation, a deep copy is made to avoid mutations, and the merged DestinationRule combines subsets from both sources but only preserves the ConfigKey from the first rule in the dependencies map.\n\nThe merging process tracks existing subset names and appends new ones from the incoming rule, skipping duplicates and recording metrics when conflicts occur.\n\nAfter merging, only the modified original rule is stored back in the list—the incoming rule itself isn't added. This means the destination rules map ends up with a single entry per hostname containing the combined subsets from both rules. When SidecarScope later iterates through the destination rules, it processes this merged version.\n\nThe critical issue emerges during dependency tracking. The code registers a ConfigKey only for the rule that remains in the list (DR-1 with its merged subsets), but never registers a dependency for the incoming rule (DR-2). So when DR-2 is subsequently updated, the change event fires for its ConfigKey, but since that key was never recorded in configDependencies, the affected proxies aren't identified for pushing. The merging logic inadvertently breaks the dependency chain for the second This is the critical path where the bug manifests.\n\nNow I have a complete understanding of the issue. Let me create the investigation report.\n\n## Summary of the Root Cause\n\n1. **How DestinationRules are merged**: In `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`, the `mergeDestinationRule()` function (line 38) merges multiple DestinationRules for the same host into a single entry in `p.destRules[resolvedHost]`. When two DRs without workload selectors target the same host, the second DR's subsets are added to the first DR, and the second DR is not added as a separate entry to the list.\n\n2. **Loss of identity metadata**: After merging, only the first DR's `config.Config` object remains in the list. The second DR's metadata (Name and Namespace) is no longer present in the consolidated structure, even though its subsets are merged into the first DR's specification.\n\n3. **SidecarScope dependency registration**: In `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`, `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` (lines 219-227) and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 410-416) iterate through `out.destinationRules[hostname]` and add `ConfigKey` entries for each DR to the `configDependencies` set. Since the merged DR only has one config.Config in the list, only one ConfigKey is registered - the one from the DR that \"won\" the merge.\n\n4. **The xDS push filter failure**: In `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`, the `ConfigAffectsProxy()` function (line 32) checks if a config change affects a proxy by calling `proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config)` (line 64). \n\nWhen a DR is updated, `DependsOnConfig()` checks whether its ConfigKey exists in the `configDependencies` set. If the modified DR lost its identity during the merge, its key won't be found, causing the method to return false and skip the xDS push entirely. The `PushContext` in `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` maintains a `destinationRuleIndex` organized by hostname, where the `destinationRule()` function retrieves these merged rules transparently to callers, masking the fact that multiple DRs have been consolidated into a single entry.\n\nThe core issue traces back through several layers: updating a secondary DestinationRule fails to notify affected proxies because that DR's ConfigKey isn't tracked in their dependencies. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01LMEqM4TozgR3btJsVV931h","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_018fZxzoxF7YvKZ3XkiDWjv4","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update\n\n## Summary\n\nWhen multiple DestinationRules for the same host are merged during configuration initialization, only the first DR's ConfigKey is registered in the proxy's dependency tracking. When the second (or subsequent) DR is updated, the xDS push filter incorrectly skips the update because the updated DR's identity was lost during merging, resulting in stale Envoy configuration.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **mismatch between the merging process and the dependency tracking mechanism**. The `mergeDestinationRule()` function in `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` consolidates multiple DRs into a single entry while discarding the identity of non-primary DRs, but the dependency tracking in `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` only registers the surviving DR's ConfigKey, not all contributing DRs.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. DestinationRule Merging (pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go)\n\n**Function**: `mergeDestinationRule()` (lines 38-109)\n\nThe function merges multiple DRs for the same host by:\n- At lines 41-104: Iterating through existing DRs (`mdrList`) for the resolved host\n- At lines 44-60: Checking if the incoming DR should be merged with an existing one\n- At lines 63-100: When `bothWithoutSelector` (both DRs lack workload selectors), the incoming DR's subsets are **added** to the existing DR (line 80), but the incoming DR itself is **not** appended to the list (line 101 skips addition when `addRuleToProcessedDestRules = false`)\n- At lines 101-103: Only if `addRuleToProcessedDestRules = true` is the incoming DR added as a separate entry\n\n**Key observation**: When two DRs without workload selectors target the same host, the second DR's specifications are merged into the first DR's object, but the second DR's `config.Config` metadata is lost. The `destRuleIndex[hostname]` list contains only one entry.\n\n### 2. Consolidated DestRules Structure (pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go)\n\n**Type**: `consolidatedDestRules` (lines 251-256)\n\n```go\ntype consolidatedDestRules struct {\n    exportTo  map[host.Name]map[visibility.Instance]bool\n    destRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config  // Maps hostname to list of DRs\n}\n```\n\nThis structure stores DRs by hostname, keyed in `destRules`. After `SetDestinationRules()` calls `mergeDestinationRule()`, this map contains only one DR entry per hostname when multiple DRs are merged.\n\n### 3. SidecarScope Dependency Registration (pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go)\n\n**DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()** (lines 219-227):\n```go\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,              // Only first DR's name registered\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,         // Only first DR's namespace registered\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**ConvertToSidecarScope()** (lines 410-416):\n```go\nfor _, dr := range drList {\n    out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n        Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n        Name:      dr.Name,                 // Only first DR's name registered\n        Namespace: dr.Namespace,            // Only first DR's namespace registered\n    })\n}\n```\n\n**Key observation**: The code iterates through `drList` (which should contain all DRs for that hostname), but after merging, the list contains only the first DR. The ConfigKey for the second DR is never registered.\n\n### 4. The DependsOnConfig Check (pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go, pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go)\n\n**DependsOnConfig()** (lines 523-540 in sidecar.go):\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    // ...\n    _, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\n    return exists\n}\n```\n\n**ConfigAffectsProxy()** (lines 32-58 in proxy_dependencies.go):\n```go\nfunc ConfigAffectsProxy(req *model.PushRequest, proxy *model.Proxy) bool {\n    if len(req.ConfigsUpdated) == 0 {\n        return true\n    }\n    for config := range req.ConfigsUpdated {\n        // ...\n        if affected && checkProxyDependencies(proxy, config) {\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\n**checkProxyDependencies()** (lines 60-74 in proxy_dependencies.go):\n```go\nfunc checkProxyDependencies(proxy *model.Proxy, config model.ConfigKey) bool {\n    switch proxy.Type {\n    case model.SidecarProxy:\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true                      // Push will be sent\n        }\n    }\n    return false                             // Push will be skipped\n}\n```\n\n**Key observation**: When a config change event occurs (e.g., updating the second DR), `ConfigAffectsProxy()` checks `DependsOnConfig()` with the updated DR's ConfigKey. If that ConfigKey was never registered due to merging, `DependsOnConfig()` returns false, and the entire push is skipped.\n\n### 5. Push Filtering (pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go)\n\n**pushConnection()** (lines 680-712):\n```go\nif !s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, pushRequest) {\n    log.Debugf(\"Skipping push to %v, no updates required\", con.conID)\n    return nil  // Push is skipped\n}\n```\n\n**ProxyNeedsPush** is set to `DefaultProxyNeedsPush()` (discovery.go line 191), which calls `ConfigAffectsProxy()` → `checkProxyDependencies()` → `DependsOnConfig()`.\n\n**Key observation**: If `DependsOnConfig()` returns false for the updated DR, the push is silently skipped at line 689, and the proxy never receives the configuration update.\n\n### 6. Scenario: Two DestinationRules for Same Host\n\n**Initial state:**\n- `reviews-traffic-policy` DR created (defines trafficPolicy)\n- `reviews-subsets` DR created (defines subsets)\n- Both target `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local` with no workload selector\n\n**After SetDestinationRules():**\n- In `mergeDestinationRule()`, when processing `reviews-subsets`, it finds `reviews-traffic-policy` already in the list\n- Since both lack workload selectors, it merges the subsets into `reviews-traffic-policy`\n- `p.destRules[hostname]` = `[reviews-traffic-policy with merged subsets]`\n- `reviews-subsets` ConfigKey is discarded\n\n**When SidecarScope is built:**\n- Only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s ConfigKey is registered in `configDependencies`\n\n**When reviews-subsets is updated (e.g., adding v3 subset):**\n- ConfigUpdate event fires with ConfigKey `{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n- ConfigAffectsProxy checks if any proxy depends on this config\n- DependsOnConfig looks for this ConfigKey in configDependencies\n- **ConfigKey not found** (only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" is registered)\n- Returns false\n- **Push is skipped**\n- Envoy continues serving stale configuration\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go**\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - Loses identity of merged DRs\n   - No tracking of which DRs contributed to a merged config\n\n2. **pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go**\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` - Only registers ConfigKeys from visible DRs in consolidated list\n   - `ConvertToSidecarScope()` - Same issue\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` - Correctly checks dependencies but receives incomplete registration\n\n3. **pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go**\n   - `SetDestinationRules()` - Calls `mergeDestinationRule()` and builds index\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - Called here at lines 1716, 1739\n   - `destinationRule()` - Returns merged DRs without indicating that multiple DRs contributed\n\n4. **pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` - Uses incomplete dependency information\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` - Relies on `DependsOnConfig()` which has incomplete data\n   - `DefaultProxyNeedsPush()` - Uses `ConfigAffectsProxy()`\n\n5. **pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go**\n   - `pushConnection()` - Line 688 calls ProxyNeedsPush which may incorrectly skip pushes\n   - Uses the proxy dependency filter to decide whether to send updates\n\n6. **pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go**\n   - `ProxyNeedsPush` function pointer set to `DefaultProxyNeedsPush`\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Updating `reviews-subsets` DestinationRule does not trigger xDS push to sidecar\n   - Evidence: `/debug/config_dump` on sidecar shows old configuration even after DR update in API server\n\n2. **Intermediate Hop 1**: ConfigAffectsProxy returns false for the updated DR\n   - Code path: `pushConnection()` (ads.go:688) → `ProxyNeedsPush()` → `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (proxy_dependencies.go:32) → returns false\n\n3. **Intermediate Hop 2**: checkProxyDependencies returns false because DependsOnConfig returns false\n   - Code path: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (proxy_dependencies.go:38-54) → `checkProxyDependencies()` (proxy_dependencies.go:60) → `DependsOnConfig()` (sidecar.go:523)\n\n4. **Intermediate Hop 3**: DependsOnConfig cannot find the updated DR's ConfigKey in configDependencies\n   - Code path: `DependsOnConfig()` (sidecar.go:538) → looks for `config.HashCode()` in `sc.configDependencies` → **not found**\n\n5. **Root Cause Mechanism**: The ConfigKey for the updated DR was never registered in configDependencies\n   - Root cause: `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` / `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416) iterate through `out.destinationRules[hostname]` and register ConfigKeys\n   - But after `SetDestinationRules()` calls `mergeDestinationRule()` (push_context.go:1716, 1739), only the first DR remains in the list\n   - The second DR's metadata is lost during `mergeDestinationRule()` (destination_rule.go:38-109) when `addRuleToProcessedDestRules = false` (line 60) and the DR is not appended (line 102-103)\n\n6. **Root Cause**: In `mergeDestinationRule()`, when two DRs without workload selectors target the same host:\n   - The incoming DR's subsets are merged into the existing DR (line 80)\n   - The incoming DR is not added to the list as a separate entry (line 101-103)\n   - Only the first DR's ConfigKey survives; subsequent DRs' identities are discarded\n   - **This violates the assumption of the dependency tracking layer**, which expects all DRs contributing to a service's configuration to be tracked\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe core issue is that the merging process destroys the identity of contributing DRs. The fix should restore identity tracking:\n\n1. **Option A - Track Contributing DRs**: Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to store a list of contributing ConfigKeys in addition to the merged DR. When SidecarScope registers dependencies, register all contributing DRs, not just the merged one.\n\n2. **Option B - Preserve DR Identity**: Change the merging strategy to keep all DR ConfigKeys in the list, not just the merged one. Modify the merging logic to avoid modifying the first DR in-place but instead create a synthetic merged DR that tracks all contributions.\n\n3. **Option C - Detect Updates on Merged Specs**: When a DestinationRule is updated, even if its ConfigKey is not in configDependencies, check if any dependency targets the same host and trigger a push for those proxies.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Monitor dependency registration**:\n   - Add logging in `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` to log all registered ConfigKeys\n   - Verify that both DRs' ConfigKeys are registered when two DRs exist for the same host\n\n2. **Trace the config update path**:\n   - Add logging in `ConfigAffectsProxy()` to log which configs are checked and their dependency status\n   - Add logging in `DependsOnConfig()` to show which ConfigKeys are in configDependencies\n\n3. **Verify the merging process**:\n   - Add logging in `mergeDestinationRule()` to show when DRs are merged vs. kept as separate entries\n   - Log the resulting `destRules` index to show which ConfigKeys survive the merge\n\n4. **Test incremental updates**:\n   - Create two DRs for the same host\n   - Update the second DR\n   - Trace the ConfigUpdate event to see which ConfigKey is sent\n   - Verify that SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig returns true for that ConfigKey\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":495,"cache_read_input_tokens":77200,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":495},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dc3bd857-3b1f-4804-8237-c78ccbb5fe87","uuid":"da0b96cb-9b5c-40e2-8c78-1aaf6c8cfd42"}

The `destRuleIndex[hostname]` list contains only one entry.\n\n### 2. Consolidated DestRules Structure (pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go)\n\n**Type**: `consolidatedDestRules` (lines 251-256)\n\n```go\ntype consolidatedDestRules struct {\n    exportTo  map[host.Name]map[visibility.Instance]bool\n    destRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config  // Maps hostname to list of DRs\n}\n```\n\nThis structure stores DRs by hostname, keyed in `destRules`. After `SetDestinationRules()` calls `mergeDestinationRule()`, this map contains only one DR entry per hostname when multiple DRs are merged.\n\n### 3. SidecarScope Dependency Registration (pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go)\n\n**DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()** (lines 219-227):\n```go\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,              // Only first DR's name registered\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,         // Only first DR's namespace registered\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**ConvertToSidecarScope()** (lines 410-416):\n```go\nfor _, dr := range drList {\n    out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n        Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n        Name:      dr.Name,                 // Only first DR's name registered\n        Namespace: dr.Namespace,            // Only first DR's namespace registered\n    })\n}\n```\n\n**Key observation**: The code iterates through `drList` (which should contain all DRs for that hostname), but after merging, the list contains only the first DR. The ConfigKey for the second DR is never registered.\n\n### 4. The DependsOnConfig Check (pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go, pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go)\n\n**DependsOnConfig()** (lines 523-540 in sidecar.go):\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    // ...\n    _, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\n    return exists\n}\n```\n\n**ConfigAffectsProxy()** (lines 32-58 in proxy_dependencies.go):\n```go\nfunc ConfigAffectsProxy(req *model.PushRequest, proxy *model.Proxy) bool {\n    if len(req.ConfigsUpdated) == 0 {\n        return true\n    }\n    for config := range req.ConfigsUpdated {\n        // ...\n        if affected && checkProxyDependencies(proxy, config) {\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\n**checkProxyDependencies()** (lines 60-74 in proxy_dependencies.go):\n```go\nfunc checkProxyDependencies(proxy *model.Proxy, config model.ConfigKey) bool {\n    switch proxy.Type {\n    case model.SidecarProxy:\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true                      // Push will be sent\n        }\n    }\n    return false                             // Push will be skipped\n}\n```\n\n**Key observation**: When a config change event occurs (e.g., updating the second DR), `ConfigAffectsProxy()` checks `DependsOnConfig()` with the updated DR's ConfigKey. If that ConfigKey was never registered due to merging, `DependsOnConfig()` returns false, and the entire push is skipped.\n\n### 5. Push Filtering (pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go)\n\n**pushConnection()** (lines 680-712):\n```go\nif !s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, pushRequest) {\n    log.Debugf(\"Skipping push to %v, no updates required\", con.conID)\n    return nil  // Push is skipped\n}\n```\n\n**ProxyNeedsPush** is set to `DefaultProxyNeedsPush()` (discovery.go line 191), which calls `ConfigAffectsProxy()` → `checkProxyDependencies()` → `DependsOnConfig()`.\n\n**Key observation**: If `DependsOnConfig()` returns false for the updated DR, the push is silently skipped at line 689, and the proxy never receives the configuration update.\n\n### 6. Scenario: Two DestinationRules for Same Host\n\n**Initial state:**\n- `reviews-traffic-policy` DR created (defines trafficPolicy)\n- `reviews-subsets` DR created (defines subsets)\n- Both target `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local` with no workload selector\n\n**After SetDestinationRules():**\n- In `mergeDestinationRule()`, when processing `reviews-subsets`, it finds `reviews-traffic-policy` already in the list\n- Since both lack workload selectors, it merges the subsets into `reviews-traffic-policy`\n- `p.destRules[hostname]` = `[reviews-traffic-policy with merged subsets]`\n- `reviews-subsets` ConfigKey is discarded\n\n**When SidecarScope is built:**\n- Only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s ConfigKey is registered in `configDependencies`\n\n**When reviews-subsets is updated (e.g., adding v3 subset):**\n- ConfigUpdate event fires with ConfigKey `{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n- ConfigAffectsProxy checks if any proxy depends on this config\n- DependsOnConfig looks for this ConfigKey in configDependencies\n- **ConfigKey not found** (only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" is registered)\n- Returns false\n- **Push is skipped**\n- Envoy continues serving stale configuration\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go**\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - Loses identity of merged DRs\n   - No tracking of which DRs contributed to a merged config\n\n2. **pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go**\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` - Only registers ConfigKeys from visible DRs in consolidated list\n   - `ConvertToSidecarScope()` - Same issue\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` - Correctly checks dependencies but receives incomplete registration\n\n3. **pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go**\n   - `SetDestinationRules()` - Calls `mergeDestinationRule()` and builds index\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - Called here at lines 1716, 1739\n   - `destinationRule()` - Returns merged DRs without indicating that multiple DRs contributed\n\n4. **pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` - Uses incomplete dependency information\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` - Relies on `DependsOnConfig()` which has incomplete data\n   - `DefaultProxyNeedsPush()` - Uses `ConfigAffectsProxy()`\n\n5. **pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go**\n   - `pushConnection()` - Line 688 calls ProxyNeedsPush which may incorrectly skip pushes\n   - Uses the proxy dependency filter to decide whether to send updates\n\n6. **pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go**\n   - `ProxyNeedsPush` function pointer set to `DefaultProxyNeedsPush`\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Updating `reviews-subsets` DestinationRule does not trigger xDS push to sidecar\n   - Evidence: `/debug/config_dump` on sidecar shows old configuration even after DR update in API server\n\n2. **Intermediate Hop 1**: ConfigAffectsProxy returns false for the updated DR\n   - Code path: `pushConnection()` (ads.go:688) → `ProxyNeedsPush()` → `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (proxy_dependencies.go:32) → returns false\n\n3. **Intermediate Hop 2**: checkProxyDependencies returns false because DependsOnConfig returns false\n   - Code path: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (proxy_dependencies.go:38-54) → `checkProxyDependencies()` (proxy_dependencies.go:60) → `DependsOnConfig()` (sidecar.go:523)\n\n4. **Intermediate Hop 3**: DependsOnConfig cannot find the updated DR's ConfigKey in configDependencies\n   - Code path: `DependsOnConfig()` (sidecar.go:538) → looks for `config.HashCode()` in `sc.configDependencies` → **not found**\n\n5. **Root Cause Mechanism**: The ConfigKey for the updated DR was never registered in configDependencies\n   - Root cause: `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` / `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416) iterate through `out.destinationRules[hostname]` and register ConfigKeys\n   - But after `SetDestinationRules()` calls `mergeDestinationRule()` (push_context.go:1716, 1739), only the first DR remains in the list\n   - The second DR's metadata is lost during `mergeDestinationRule()` (destination_rule.go:38-109) when `addRuleToProcessedDestRules = false` (line 60) and the DR is not appended (line 102-103)\n\n6. **Root Cause**: In `mergeDestinationRule()`, when two DRs without workload selectors target the same host:\n   - The incoming DR's subsets are merged into the existing DR (line 80)\n   - The incoming DR is not added to the list as a separate entry (line 101-103)\n   - Only the first DR's ConfigKey survives; subsequent DRs' identities are discarded\n   - **This violates the assumption of the dependency tracking layer**, which expects all DRs contributing to a service's configuration to be tracked\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe core issue is that the merging process destroys the identity of contributing DRs. The fix should restore identity tracking:\n\n1. **Option A - Track Contributing DRs**: Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to store a list of contributing ConfigKeys in addition to the merged DR. When SidecarScope registers dependencies, register all contributing DRs, not just the merged one.\n\n2. **Option B - Preserve DR Identity**: Change the merging strategy to keep all DR ConfigKeys in the list, not just the merged one. Modify the merging logic to avoid modifying the first DR in-place but instead create a synthetic merged DR that tracks all contributions.\n\n3. **Option C - Detect Updates on Merged Specs**: When a DestinationRule is updated, even if its ConfigKey is not in configDependencies, check if any dependency targets the same host and trigger a push for those proxies.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Monitor dependency registration**:\n   - Add logging in `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` to log all registered ConfigKeys\n   - Verify that both DRs' ConfigKeys are registered when two DRs exist for the same host\n\n2. **Trace the config update path**:\n   - Add logging in `ConfigAffectsProxy()` to log which configs are checked and their dependency status\n   - Add logging in `DependsOnConfig()` to show which ConfigKeys are in configDependencies\n\n3. **Verify the merging process**:\n   - Add logging in `mergeDestinationRule()` to show when DRs are merged vs. kept as separate entries\n   - Log the resulting `destRules` index to show which ConfigKeys survive the merge\n\n4. **Test incremental updates**:\n   - Create two DRs for the same host\n   - Update the second DR\n   - Trace the ConfigUpdate event to see which ConfigKey is sent\n   - Verify that SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig returns true for that ConfigKey\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
